<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="point-to-ponder">POINT TO PONDER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#point-to-ponder" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Many nurses are in poor physical condition, smoke, regularly eat junk foods, take little time for themselves, and demonstrate other unhealthy habits. What do you think are some of the reasons for this? What can be done to improve nurses' health habits?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="educate-caregivers">Educate Caregivers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#educate-caregivers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Be it the nursing director, a family member who cares for an older relative, a health aide who has more frequent contact with the patient than the professional nurse, or the physician who only occasionally has an older person in the caseload, caregivers at every level require competency in providing services to the older population. Gerontological nurses can influence the education of caregivers by:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Helping nursing schools identify relevant issues for inclusion in the curricula</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Participating in the classroom and field experiences of students</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Evaluating educational deficits of personnel and planning educational experiences to eliminate deficits</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Promoting interdisciplinary team conferences</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Attending and participating in continuing education programs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reading current nursing literature and sharing information with colleagues</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Serving as a role model by demonstrating current practices</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>With increasing numbers of family members providing more complex care in the home setting than ever before, it is essential that the education of this group not be overlooked. It should not be assumed that because the family has had contact with other providers or has been providing care they are knowledgeable in correct care techniques. The nurse must periodically evaluate and reinforce the family's knowledge and skills.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="develop-new-roles">Develop New Roles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#develop-new-roles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As gerontological subspecialties and settings for care grow, so will the opportunities for nurses to carve new roles for themselves. Nurses can demonstrate creativity and leadership as they break from traditional roles and settings and develop new models of practice, which may include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Geropsychiatric nurse specialist in the continuing care retirement community setting</li>
<li>Independent case manager for community-based chronically ill patients</li>
<li>Columnist for local newspaper on issues pertaining to health and aging</li>
<li>Owner or director of mature women’s health care center, geriatric day care program, respite agency, or caregiver training center</li>
<li>Preretirement counselor and educator for private industry</li>
<li>Faith community nurse</li>
<li>Consultant, educator, and case manager for geriatric surgical patients</li>
</ul>
<p>This list only begins to describe opportunities awaiting gerontological nurses. Many opportunities exist for nurses to develop new practice models in gerontological care. It will be important for gerontological nurses to identify nontraditional roles, approach them creatively, test innovative practice models, and share their successes and failures with colleagues to aid them in their development of new roles. Nurses must recognize that their biopsychosocial sciences knowledge, clinical competencies, and human relations skills give them a strong competitive edge over other disciplines in affecting a wide range of services.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>POINT TO PONDER</p>
<p>Based on changes in the health care system and society at large, what unique services could gerontological nurses offer in the future within your community?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="balance-quality-care-and-health-care-costs">Balance Quality Care and Health Care Costs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#balance-quality-care-and-health-care-costs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The growing number of older adults is placing increasing demands for diverse health care services than ever before. At the same time, third-party insurers are trying to control the constantly escalating cost of services. Earlier hospital discharges, limited home health visits, increased complexity of nursing home residents, and greater out-of-pocket payment for services by patients demonstrate some of the effects of changes in reimbursement policy. There is concern that, as a result of these changes, patients are discharged from hospitals prematurely and suffer greater adverse consequences, nursing homes are confronting residents with complex problems for whom they are not adequately prepared or staffed, families are being strained by considerable caregiving burdens, and patients are being deprived of needed but unaffordable services.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251227-472b7396.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="concept-mastery-alert">Concept Mastery Alert<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#concept-mastery-alert" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Changes in reimbursement practices result in the earlier hospital discharge of patients with high acuity level care needs. The limited reimbursement for nursing home and home health care services may not provide the resources to adequately provide the type of care required by these individuals.</p>
<p>Such changes are disconcerting and may cause nurses to feel overwhelmed, frustrated, or dissatisfied. Unfortunately, more cost cutting is likely to occur. Rather than experience burnout or consider a change of</p>
<p>occupation, nurses should become involved in cost-containment efforts so that a balance between quality services and budgetary concerns can be achieved. Efforts toward this goal can include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Test creative staffing patterns. Perhaps six nurses can be more productive than three nurses and three unlicensed caregivers. Or, perhaps some of the high nonproductive time costs associated with unlicensed personnel are related to poor hiring and supervision practices; improved management techniques may increase the cost-effectiveness of these workers.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Use lay caregivers. Neighbors assisting each other, a family member rooming-in during hospitalizations, and other methods to increase the resources available for service provision can be explored.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Abolish unnecessary practices. Why must nurses spend time administering medications to patients who have successfully administered them before admission and who will continue to administer them after discharge, take vital signs every 4 hours on patients who have shown no abnormalities, bathe all patients on the same schedule regardless of skin condition or state of cleanliness, or rewrite assessments and care plans at specified intervals regardless of a patient's changes or stability? Often regulations and policies are developed under the assumption that, without them, vital signs would never be taken, baths would not be given, and other facets of care would not be completed. Perhaps the time has come for nurses to aggressively convince others that they have the professional judgment to determine the need for and frequency of assessment, care planning, and care delivery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure safe care. The implementation of cost-containment efforts should be accompanied by concurrent studies of its impact on rates of complications, readmissions, incidents, consumer satisfaction, and staff turnover, absenteeism, and morale. Specific numbers and documented cases carry more weight than broad criticisms or complaints that care is suffering.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Advocate for older adults. The priorities of society and professions change. History shows us that at different times, the spotlight has focused on various underserved groups, such as children, pregnant women, the mentally ill, the disabled, substance abusers, and, most</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>recently, older adults. As interests and priorities shift to new groups, gerontological nurses must make certain that the needs of older individuals are not forgotten or shortchanged.</p>
<p>As gerontological nursing continues to shed its image of a less-than-challenging specialty for less-than-competent nurses and fully emerges as the dynamic, multifaceted, and opportunity-filled area of nursing that it is, it will be recognized as a specialty for the finest talent the profession has to offer. Gerontological nursing has just begun to show its true potential.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bringing-research-to-life">BRINGING RESEARCH TO LIFE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bringing-research-to-life" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="knowledge-and-perceptions-about-aging-and-frailty-an-integrative-review-of-the-literature">Knowledge and Perceptions About Aging and Frailty: An Integrative Review of the Literature<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#knowledge-and-perceptions-about-aging-and-frailty-an-integrative-review-of-the-literature" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Source: Parish, A., Kim, J., Lewallen, K. M., Miller, S., Myers, J., Panepinto, R., et al. (2019). Geriatric Nursing, 40 (1), 13–24.</p>
<p>Hypothesizing that community-based adults have a poor understanding of the concept of frailty and that little information exists describing this lack of knowledge, this research, conducted by a team of nurses, aimed to do an integrative review to create a conceptual model that presented a description of public knowledge and perceptions of aging and frailty.</p>
<p>Twenty-three studies (6 quantitative, 11 qualitative, and 6 mixed-methods) were included in the review. Of the studies:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>None characterized the relationship between knowledge and perceptions of aging and health behaviors.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Two found a relationship between stereotypes about aging and aging-related anxiety.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There was an underexploration of the relationship between older adults’ values and knowledge of aging and health behaviors.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>None linked perceptions of aging with measured health behaviors, although some studies described the manner in which an individual’s perception of aspects that affect aging influence health behaviors.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Only two studies addressed lay perceptions of frailty; participants viewed frailty holistically, affecting all aspects of a person.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The authors concluded that greater understanding of aging and frailty from a scientific perspective is needed.</p>
<p>This study reinforces the importance of the gerontological nurse's roles as educator and advocate. Despite considerable information about factors influencing aging and frailty, the average lay person lacks information about this relationship. The gerontological nurse can explore opportunities to educate lay people (e.g., via community fairs, articles in lay magazines, presentations at social group functions, etc.). In addition, nurses can advocate for more research into how the relationship of knowledge about aging and frailty affects health behaviors, as well as interventions to enhance consumer knowledge.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="practice-realities">PRACTICE REALITIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#practice-realities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Nurse Yen is a new graduate of a BSN program who has joined the staff of a subacute care unit of the local hospital. Most of the nurses on staff are diplomas and ADN graduates who have been out of school for more than a decade.</p>
<p>Ms. Yen notices that some of the nurses are unaware of current best practices and trends. In informal conversations, she has learned that none of the nurses subscribes to professional journals or belongs to a professional association, and the rare times they have attended continuing education programs was when the hospital sent them.</p>
<p>What can Nurse Yen do to help these nurses understand the importance and engage in continuing education?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="critical-thinking-exercises">CRITICAL THINKING EXERCISES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#critical-thinking-exercises" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>What were some of the reasons for the poor status of gerontological nursing in the past?</li>
<li>Why is the nursing role of healer particularly meaningful to gerontological practice?</li>
<li>What theme regarding the involvement of the older adult is apparent in the ANA Standards of the Gerontological Nurse?</li>
<li>Describe several issues that could warrant gerontological nursing research activities.</li>
<li>Describe how the increased use of holistic practices could have a positive effect on cost and consumer satisfaction.</li>
<li>Outline functions that could be performed by a gerontological nurse in the roles of (a) assisted-living community preadmission health screener, (b) health counselor in a retirement community, (c) caregiver trainer, (d) industrial preretirement health educator, and (e) faith community nurse.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-summary">Chapter Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Although nurses have a long history of caring for older adults, the formal creation of a specialty of gerontological nursing did not occur until the 1970s. Since that time the specialty has grown considerably with the creation of standards, clarification of competencies, and development of several organizations that address the unique needs of nurses in this specialty. As the specialty has developed, there has been differentiation between geriatric nursing, which involves the nursing care of sick older adults, and gerontological nursing, which promotes wellness and healthy aging for all individuals.</p>
<p>The major roles for gerontological nurses include that of healer, caregiver, educator, advocate, and innovator. There also are advanced practice roles for nurses in this specialty.</p>
<p>To effectively care for others, gerontological nurses must care for themselves. This includes positive health care practices, having positive connections with others, attending to spiritual needs, and taking time for self. These practices not only promote health in nurses themselves but enable nurses to serve as models of healthy aging practices to others.</p>
<p>Gerontological nurses face challenges as the specialty continues to grow, such as assuring practice is based on evidence, advancing research, promoting integrative care, educating caregivers, developing new roles within the specialty, and balancing quality care with pressures to control health care costs.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-7">CHAPTER 7<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-7" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="holistic-assessment-and-care-planning">Holistic Assessment and Care Planning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#holistic-assessment-and-care-planning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-outline">Chapter Outline<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-outline" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
